    \section{\texorpdfstring{\href{https://github.com/LTS5/iapr-2018}{IAPR
2018:} Lab 2 ‒ Object
description}{IAPR 2018: Lab 2 ‒ Object description}}\label{iapr-2018iapr2018-lab-2-object-description}

\textbf{Author:} Axel Manguy \textbf{Due date:} 04.05.2018

    \subsection{Extract relevant data}\label{extract-relevant-data}

We first need to extract the \texttt{lab-02-data.tar.gz} archive. To
this end, we use the
\href{https://docs.python.org/3.6/library/tarfile.html}{tarfile} module
from the Python standard library.

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}1}]:} \PY{k+kn}{import} \PY{n+nn}{tarfile}
        \PY{k+kn}{import} \PY{n+nn}{os}
        
        \PY{n}{data\PYZus{}base\PYZus{}path} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{os}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{path}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{join}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{os}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{pardir}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{data}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{)}
        \PY{n}{data\PYZus{}folder} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{lab\PYZhy{}02\PYZhy{}data}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}
        \PY{n}{tar\PYZus{}path} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{os}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{path}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{join}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{data\PYZus{}base\PYZus{}path}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{data\PYZus{}folder} \PY{o}{+} \PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{.tar.gz}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{)}
        \PY{k}{with} \PY{n}{tarfile}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{open}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{tar\PYZus{}path}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{mode}\PY{o}{=}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{r:gz}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{)} \PY{k}{as} \PY{n}{tar}\PY{p}{:}
            \PY{n}{tar}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{extractall}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{path}\PY{o}{=}\PY{n}{data\PYZus{}base\PYZus{}path}\PY{p}{)}
\end{Verbatim}


    \subsection{Part 1}\label{part-1}

In the \texttt{lab-02-data/part1} folder, you will find 28x28 grey-scale
pictures of handwritten "0" and "1". These digits have been extracted
from MNIST dataset (http://yann.lecun.com/exdb/mnist/).

Your goal is to extract, from each of those images, a 2-dimensional
feature vector (i.e. 2 features) and to plot them all on a 2D graph. If
you have chosen good features, the vectors of the "0"'s should nicely
cluster in one part of the plane and those of the "1"'s in another.

Please try first the Fourier Descriptors. You can make several attempts:
e.g. with and without invariance to rotation, translation, scaling, etc.
You can also for instance rotate the images and assess the invariance in
rotation.

\textbf{Note:} for the Fourier descriptors, the u\_k signal has to be
constructed by following the contour point after point. Some
pre-processing (image binarization, possibly some Mathematical
Morphology) might be useful.

Then feel free to try other features, the more you try, the better it
will be (for you).

    \subsubsection{1.1 Data visualization and contour
spectrum}\label{data-visualization-and-contour-spectrum}

Before doing any operation on a images, and since we're going to extract
frequencies, one first idea is to look at the spectrum of each contour.
Using the marching square algorythm through the find\_contour method
from skimage (details in section 1.2.2), we plot the amplitude for the
10 first frequency. It appears that the first frequency performs well at
distinguiching 0 from 1. All other frequency will not be relavant
feature for that task.

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}81}]:} \PY{k+kn}{import} \PY{n+nn}{skimage}\PY{n+nn}{.}\PY{n+nn}{io}
         \PY{k+kn}{from} \PY{n+nn}{skimage} \PY{k}{import} \PY{n}{measure}
         \PY{k+kn}{from} \PY{n+nn}{skimage} \PY{k}{import} \PY{n}{feature}
         \PY{k+kn}{from} \PY{n+nn}{skimage} \PY{k}{import} \PY{n}{filters}
         \PY{k+kn}{from} \PY{n+nn}{skimage} \PY{k}{import} \PY{n}{morphology}
         \PY{k+kn}{from} \PY{n+nn}{skimage}\PY{n+nn}{.}\PY{n+nn}{filters} \PY{k}{import} \PY{n}{gaussian}

    \subsubsection{1.2 Fourier descriptors}\label{fourier-descriptors}

Two different methods are tested for finding a contour. Since we're
doing fourrier descriptors we need a contour that progress along the
shape with a starting point and an end so we can convert it into a
relevant signal. The two methods we found for that purpose are
active\_contour (a minimising energy method) and find\_contour (a
marching square method).

    \paragraph{1.2.2 Fourier descriptors :
active\_contour}\label{fourier-descriptors-active_contour}

One main drawback of the active\_contour method is the difficulty to
find the good set of parameters that will achive the task. In order to
help the function giving the right contour, we skeletonize the initial
shape before a gaussian filter so the center of shape appears bright and
the edges more blur. This way, the snake will be atracted by the center
of the shape rather than the details of its border. This is esspecially
usefull for 1\_5 and 1\_9 thant have an odd shape. For these images, the
method performs well and is able to extract some abstract shape of a one
(just a straight line with thickness and orientation). However, the
method is still doing mistakes on 1\_8 taking a noise for a part of the
shape. Since there is very few pixels, The morphology operations we
tried was destroying to much of the shape to be able to retrieve
contour, so we decide to not implement then.

By performing a fourier transform on images, we can extract f1 and f2.
Without the phase and f0, the descriptors we selected are translation
and rotation invariant. The rotation invariant is relavant since the one
shapes can be inclined. Since all image have the same size and all shape
more or less the same scale being scaling invariant is not that much
important. However, and as expected the use of f1 is enough to
discriminate one and zeros.

             \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}signal creation}
             \PY{n}{signal} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{snake\PYZus{}sk}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]}\PY{o}{+}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{n}{j}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{snake\PYZus{}sk}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}
             
             \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}fourier transform}
             \PY{n}{fourier}\PY{o}{=}\PY{n}{fft}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{signal}\PY{p}{)}
             
             \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}2 first coef extraction}
             \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}abs to get to module invariant to rotation}
             \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}not taking f0 to be invariant to translation}

f1 and f2 :intra-class variance for zeros: 0.43 and  0.35
f1 and f2 :intra-class variance for ones : 0.07 and  1.65

    \end{Verbatim}

    \paragraph{1.2.2 Fourier descriptors :
find\_contour}\label{fourier-descriptors-find_contour}

Even if the previous method was performing well on finding contour, we
also wanted to tried a method that take the whole shape into account.
Especially for the ones, only taking the straight line in the center
delete some information that could be usefull for other recognition. The
find contour method works by diving the area into a grid and performing
a linear interpolation. For each cell of the grid, the marching square
method looks at the grayscale value of each corner to define the
isoline. In our case the isoline will be the contour we're searching
for.

The method for feature extraction is the same as before, we first
contruct the signal base on the contour. perform a fourier transform on
that signal and take f1 and f2 as descriptors. The results are the same
as before except, the intraclass variance is a litllte bit beter for
zeros. Since we are taking the whole shape of the ones, the intra-class
variance for the ones is higher due to 1\_5 and 1-9.

In order to compare the two method, we used normalization on data so the
variance computation is done on the same scale.

    \subsubsection{1.4 Region Based
Descriptors}\label{region-based-descriptors}

For region based descriptors 3 different couples of descriptors have
been tried. The region is extracted through The first couple is
performing well and both area and perimeters are features that can be
used on their own to perform the detection (with a simple threshold).

    \subsection{Part 2}\label{part-2}

The \texttt{lab-02-data/part2} folder contains grey-scale pictures of
handwritten "2" and "3". Extract the same feature (typically 2 Fourier
descriptors) as in part 1 also on these images and plot them on the same
graph as the features of the "0" and "1". Is it possible to discriminate
all these 4 digits with a 2-dimensional feature vector?

    \subsubsection{1.1 Data visualization}\label{data-visualization}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]

{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}37}]:} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}From my own interpretation}
         \PY{k}{def} \PY{n+nf}{contour2path}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{contour}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
             \PY{n}{path}\PY{o}{=}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{]}
             \PY{n}{directions} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{array}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{,}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{[}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{[}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{[}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}
             \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{pos} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{enumerate}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{contour}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
                 \PY{k}{if} \PY{n}{i} \PY{o}{==} \PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{contour}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{:}
                     \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{path}
                 \PY{n}{newpos} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{pos} \PY{o}{+} \PY{n}{directions}
                 \PY{n}{dist} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{sum}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{abs}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{array}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{contour}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{o}{+}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{n}{newpos}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{)}

         \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}                      From wikipedia}
         \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wagner\PYZpc{}E2\PYZpc{}80\PYZpc{}93Fischer\PYZus{}algorithm}
         \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}}
         \PY{k}{def} \PY{n+nf}{edit\PYZus{}distance}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{path1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n}{path2}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
             \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}For all i and j, d[i,j] will hold the Levenshtein distance between}
             \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} the first i characters of s and the first j characters of t.}
             \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} Note that d has (m+1) x (n+1) values.}
             \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}let d be a 2\PYZhy{}d array of int with dimensions [0..m, 0..n]}
             \PY{n}{d}\PY{o}{=}\PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{zeros}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{path1}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{+}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{path2}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{+}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
             \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{i} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{path1}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{+}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
                 \PY{n}{d}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{i} 
                 \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} the distance of any first string to an empty second string}
                 \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} (transforming the string of the first i characters of s into}
                 \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} the empty string requires i deletions)}
             \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{j} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{path2}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{+}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
                 \PY{n}{d}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{j} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} the distance of any second string to an empty first string}
           
             \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{j} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{path2}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{+}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
                 \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{i} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{range}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{path1}\PY{p}{)}\PY{o}{+}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{:}
                     \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{}print(i,j)}
                     \PY{k}{if} \PY{n}{path1}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{==} \PY{n}{path2}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{j}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]} \PY{p}{:}
                         \PY{n}{d}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{d}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{j}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]} \PY{c+c1}{\PYZsh{} no operation required}
                     \PY{k}{else}\PY{p}{:}
                         \PY{n}{d}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{min}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{d}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{j}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{+} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,}
                                           \PY{n}{d}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{j}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{+} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,}
                                           \PY{n}{d}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{i}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{j}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{+} \PY{l+m+mi}{1}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}
             \PY{k}{return} \PY{n}{d}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{path1}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{,}\PY{n+nb}{len}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{path2}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{]}
         \PY{n+nb}{print}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{edit\PYZus{}distance}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{saturda}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s+s1}{sunday}\PY{l+s+s1}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{)}
